\DoxyCodeLine{208 \textcolor{keyword}{template}<\textcolor{keyword}{typename} T>}
\DoxyCodeLine{209 \textcolor{keyword}{using }is\_unscoped\_enum =}
\DoxyCodeLine{210     std::integral\_constant<bool, std::is\_convertible<T, int>::value and}
\DoxyCodeLine{211     std::is\_enum<T>::value>;}
\DoxyCodeLine{212 }
\DoxyCodeLine{213 \textcolor{comment}{/*}}
\DoxyCodeLine{214 \textcolor{comment}{Implementation of two C++17 constructs: conjunction, negation. This is needed}}
\DoxyCodeLine{215 \textcolor{comment}{to avoid evaluating all the traits in a condition}}
\DoxyCodeLine{216 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{217 \textcolor{comment}{For example: not std::is\_same<void, T>::value and has\_value\_type<T>::value}}
\DoxyCodeLine{218 \textcolor{comment}{will not compile when T = void (on MSVC at least). Whereas}}
\DoxyCodeLine{219 \textcolor{comment}{conjunction<negation<std::is\_same<void, T>>, has\_value\_type<T>>::value will}}
\DoxyCodeLine{220 \textcolor{comment}{stop evaluating if negation<...>::value == false}}
\DoxyCodeLine{221 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{222 \textcolor{comment}{Please note that those constructs must be used with caution, since symbols can}}
\DoxyCodeLine{223 \textcolor{comment}{become very long quickly (which can slow down compilation and cause MSVC}}
\DoxyCodeLine{224 \textcolor{comment}{internal compiler errors). Only use it when you have to (see example ahead).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{225 \textcolor{comment}{*/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{226 \textcolor{keyword}{template}<\textcolor{keyword}{class}...> \textcolor{keyword}{struct }\mbox{\hyperlink{structnlohmann_1_1detail_1_1conjunction}{conjunction}} : std::true\_type \{\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{227 \textcolor{keyword}{template}<\textcolor{keyword}{class} B1> \textcolor{keyword}{struct }\mbox{\hyperlink{structnlohmann_1_1detail_1_1conjunction}{conjunction<B1>}} : B1 \{\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{228 \textcolor{keyword}{template}<\textcolor{keyword}{class }B1, \textcolor{keyword}{class}... Bn>}
\DoxyCodeLine{229 \textcolor{keyword}{struct }\mbox{\hyperlink{structnlohmann_1_1detail_1_1conjunction}{conjunction}}<B1, Bn...> : std::conditional<bool(B1::value), conjunction<Bn...>, B1>::type \{\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{230 }
\DoxyCodeLine{231 \textcolor{keyword}{template}<\textcolor{keyword}{class} B> \textcolor{keyword}{struct }\mbox{\hyperlink{structnlohmann_1_1detail_1_1negation}{negation}} : std::integral\_constant < bool, !B::value > \{\};}

\DoxyCodeLine{7152 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7153     \textcolor{comment}{/*}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7154 \textcolor{comment}{    @brief checks if given lengths do not exceed the size of a given vector}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7155 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7156 \textcolor{comment}{    To secure the access to the byte vector during CBOR/MessagePack}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7157 \textcolor{comment}{    deserialization, bytes are copied from the vector into buffers. This}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7158 \textcolor{comment}{    function checks if the number of bytes to copy (@a len) does not exceed}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7159 \textcolor{comment}{    the size @s size of the vector. Additionally, an @a offset is given from}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7160 \textcolor{comment}{    where to start reading the bytes.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7161 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7162 \textcolor{comment}{    This function checks whether reading the bytes is safe; that is, offset is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7163 \textcolor{comment}{    a valid index in the vector, offset+len}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7164 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7165 \textcolor{comment}{    @param[in] size    size of the byte vector}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7166 \textcolor{comment}{    @param[in] len     number of bytes to read}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7167 \textcolor{comment}{    @param[in] offset  offset where to start reading}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7168 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7169 \textcolor{comment}{    vec:  x x x x x X X X X X}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7170 \textcolor{comment}{          \string^         \string^         \string^}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7171 \textcolor{comment}{          0         offset    len}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7172 \textcolor{comment}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7173 \textcolor{comment}{    @throws out\_of\_range if `len > v.size()`}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7174 \textcolor{comment}{    */}}

\DoxyCodeLine{7181         \}}

\DoxyCodeLine{7183         \textcolor{comment}{// second case: adding offset would result in overflow}}

\DoxyCodeLine{7855             \textcolor{keywordflow}{case} 0xf9: \textcolor{comment}{// Half-\/Precision Float (two-\/byte IEEE 754)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7856             \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{7857                 idx += 2; \textcolor{comment}{// skip two content bytes}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7858 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7859                 \textcolor{comment}{// code from RFC 7049, Appendix D, Figure 3:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7860                 \textcolor{comment}{// As half-\/precision floating-\/point numbers were only added to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7861                 \textcolor{comment}{// IEEE 754 in 2008, today's programming platforms often still}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7862                 \textcolor{comment}{// only have limited support for them. It is very easy to}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7863                 \textcolor{comment}{// include at least decoding support for them even without such}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7864                 \textcolor{comment}{// support. An example of a small decoder for half-\/precision}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7865                 \textcolor{comment}{// floating-\/point numbers in the C language is shown in Fig. 3.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7866                 \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{int} half = (v.at(current\_idx + 1) << 8) + v.\mbox{\hyperlink{classnlohmann_1_1basic__json_a73ae333487310e3302135189ce8ff5d8}{at}}(current\_idx + 2);}
\DoxyCodeLine{7867                 \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{int} exp = (half >> 10) \& 0x1f;}
\DoxyCodeLine{7868                 \textcolor{keyword}{const} \textcolor{keywordtype}{int} mant = half \& 0x3ff;}
\DoxyCodeLine{7869                 \textcolor{keywordtype}{double} val;}
\DoxyCodeLine{7870                 \textcolor{keywordflow}{if} (exp == 0)}
\DoxyCodeLine{7871                 \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{7872                     val = std::ldexp(mant, -\/24);}
\DoxyCodeLine{7873                 \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7874                 \textcolor{keywordflow}{else} \textcolor{keywordflow}{if} (exp != 31)}
\DoxyCodeLine{7875                 \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{7876                     val = std::ldexp(mant + 1024, exp -\/ 25);}
\DoxyCodeLine{7877                 \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7878                 \textcolor{keywordflow}{else}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7879                 \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{7880                     val = mant == 0}
\DoxyCodeLine{7881                           ? std::numeric\_limits<double>::infinity()}
\DoxyCodeLine{7882                           : std::numeric\_limits<double>::quiet\_NaN();}
\DoxyCodeLine{7883                 \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7884                 \textcolor{keywordflow}{return} (half \& 0x8000) != 0 ? -\/val : val;}
\DoxyCodeLine{7885             \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{7886 }
\DoxyCodeLine{7887             \textcolor{keywordflow}{case} 0xfa: \textcolor{comment}{// Single-\/Precision Float (four-\/byte IEEE 754)}}

\DoxyCodeLine{9647         \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{9648             \textcolor{comment}{// calculate the code point from the given code points}}
\DoxyCodeLine{9649             std::size\_t codepoint = codepoint1;}
\DoxyCodeLine{9650 }
\DoxyCodeLine{9651             \textcolor{comment}{// check if codepoint1 is a high surrogate}}
\DoxyCodeLine{9652             \textcolor{keywordflow}{if} (codepoint1 >= 0xD800 and codepoint1 <= 0xDBFF)}
\DoxyCodeLine{9653             \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{9654                 \textcolor{comment}{// check if codepoint2 is a low surrogate}}
\DoxyCodeLine{9655                 \textcolor{keywordflow}{if} (codepoint2 >= 0xDC00 and codepoint2 <= 0xDFFF)}
\DoxyCodeLine{9656                 \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{9657                     codepoint =}
\DoxyCodeLine{9658                         \textcolor{comment}{// high surrogate occupies the most significant 22 bits}}
\DoxyCodeLine{9659                         (codepoint1 << 10)}
\DoxyCodeLine{9660                         \textcolor{comment}{// low surrogate occupies the least significant 15 bits}}
\DoxyCodeLine{9661                         + codepoint2}
\DoxyCodeLine{9662                         \textcolor{comment}{// there is still the 0xD800, 0xDC00 and 0x10000 noise}}
\DoxyCodeLine{9663                         \textcolor{comment}{// in the result so we have to subtract with:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{9664                         \textcolor{comment}{// (0xD800 << 10) + DC00 -\/ 0x10000 = 0x35FDC00}}
\DoxyCodeLine{9665                         -\/ 0x35FDC00;}
\DoxyCodeLine{9666                 \}}

\DoxyCodeLine{9668                 \{}

\DoxyCodeLine{9670                 \}}

\DoxyCodeLine{12029         \textcolor{keyword}{static} std::vector<std::string> \mbox{\hyperlink{classnlohmann_1_1basic__json_1_1json__pointer_ac0947d2ea20af4facc9beb07a2f30e58}{split}}(\textcolor{keyword}{const} std::string\& reference\_string)}

\DoxyCodeLine{12031             std::vector<std::string> result;}
\DoxyCodeLine{12032 }
\DoxyCodeLine{12033             \textcolor{comment}{// special case: empty reference string -\/> no reference tokens}}

\DoxyCodeLine{12035             \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{12036                 \textcolor{keywordflow}{return} result;}
\DoxyCodeLine{12037             \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12038 }
\DoxyCodeLine{12039             \textcolor{comment}{// check if nonempty reference string begins with slash}}

\DoxyCodeLine{12041             \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{12042                 JSON\_THROW(std::domain\_error(\textcolor{stringliteral}{"{}JSON pointer must be empty or begin with '/'"{}}));}
\DoxyCodeLine{12043             \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12044 }
\DoxyCodeLine{12045             \textcolor{comment}{// extract the reference tokens:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12046             \textcolor{comment}{// -\/ slash: position of the last read slash (or end of string)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12047             \textcolor{comment}{// -\/ start: position after the previous slash}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12048             \textcolor{keywordflow}{for} (}
\DoxyCodeLine{12049                 \textcolor{comment}{// search for the first slash after the first character}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12050                 \textcolor{keywordtype}{size\_t} slash = reference\_string.find\_first\_of(\textcolor{charliteral}{'/'}, 1),}
\DoxyCodeLine{12051                 \textcolor{comment}{// set the beginning of the first reference token}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12052                 start = 1;}
\DoxyCodeLine{12053                 \textcolor{comment}{// we can stop if start == string::npos+1 = 0}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12054                 start != 0;}
\DoxyCodeLine{12055                 \textcolor{comment}{// set the beginning of the next reference token}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12056                 \textcolor{comment}{// (will eventually be 0 if slash == std::string::npos)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12057                 start = slash + 1,}
\DoxyCodeLine{12058                 \textcolor{comment}{// find next slash}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12059                 slash = reference\_string.find\_first\_of(\textcolor{charliteral}{'/'}, start))}
\DoxyCodeLine{12060             \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{12061                 \textcolor{comment}{// use the text between the beginning of the reference token}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12062                 \textcolor{comment}{// (start) and the last slash (slash).}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12063                 \textcolor{keyword}{auto} reference\_token = reference\_string.substr(start, slash -\/ start);}
\DoxyCodeLine{12064 }
\DoxyCodeLine{12065                 \textcolor{comment}{// check reference tokens are properly escaped}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12066                 \textcolor{keywordflow}{for} (\textcolor{keywordtype}{size\_t} pos = reference\_token.find\_first\_of(\textcolor{charliteral}{'\string~'});}
\DoxyCodeLine{12067                         pos != std::string::npos;}
\DoxyCodeLine{12068                         pos = reference\_token.find\_first\_of(\textcolor{charliteral}{'\string~'}, pos + 1))}
\DoxyCodeLine{12069                 \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{12070                     assert(reference\_token[pos] == \textcolor{charliteral}{'\string~'});}
\DoxyCodeLine{12071 }
\DoxyCodeLine{12072                     \textcolor{comment}{// \string~ must be followed by 0 or 1}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12073                     \textcolor{keywordflow}{if} (pos == reference\_token.size() -\/ 1 or}
\DoxyCodeLine{12074                             (reference\_token[pos + 1] != \textcolor{charliteral}{'0'} and}

\DoxyCodeLine{12077                         JSON\_THROW(std::domain\_error(\textcolor{stringliteral}{"{}escape error: '\string~' must be followed with '0' or '1'"{}}));}
\DoxyCodeLine{12078                     \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12079                 \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12080 }

\DoxyCodeLine{12083                 result.push\_back(reference\_token);}
\DoxyCodeLine{12084             \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{12085 }

\DoxyCodeLine{12087         \}}
